She told me &quot;I&#39;ll come and pick you up, I have a surprise&quot;...I didn&#39;t realize how huge it was. He wanted to buy a part of the collection of vintage carrousels for Neverland. Well, with my Bat Mitsva, too :) I bragged about it the day after, but no one believed me. Kids can be so mean. It taught me some of the greatest things need to stay inside. But hey, I&#39;m a grown woman now, I can share if I want to...He was such a sweet man, and will stay the timeless genius I had the chance to ride carousels with, one sunny afternoon in Paris. click:asoqfe;" jsmodel="hc6Ubd iMhCXb"><h2 class="w1lGAd" tabindex="-1" jsaction="click:cmzydf" aria-labelledby="explanation:i60 delimiter:i60 author:i60 delimiter:i60 body:i60 delimiter:i60 info:i60"></h2><div class="XKpoMd"><span id="delimiter:i60"> </span><span id="info:i60"></span></div><div class="VBbAsb"></div><div jsname="WsjYwc" class="Ihwked UB0dDd GcESAf XkfHGe  hE2QI wQqyXe" data-iid="z13oz53qusn5gjajw04ce3h5wnrtszshdes" jsaction="click:cmzydf" jslog="6941; 1:z13oz53qusn5gjajw04ce3h5wnrtszshdes; track:impression,click" tabindex="-1"><div class="ELUvyf l7Q68c"><div jsname="uwfEUd" id="body:i60"><div class="wftCae" jsname="EjRJtf" dir="ltr">Wednesday media consumption roundup...<br><br>Books<br>Fiction: finished &quot;Girl Reading&quot;, Katie Ward. I enjoyed this, each of the vignettes was long enough to be a satisfying story, and characters were all very distinct.  I did lose the thread a bit in the last one tho, so while I had a sense that it was all supposed to cohere into one thing it didn&#39;t quite gel for me.  Started reading &quot;Reamde&quot;, Neal Stephenson, so a bit of mental whiplash from the change of style ;)  (I&#39;m reading my way through a small handful of books we bought a while ago that I haven&#39;t read).<br><br>Non-fiction: still reading Gerald Harriss&#39;s &quot;Shaping the Nation: England 1360-1461&quot; - tensions between the leadership of the towns &amp; the general populace, and how this didn&#39;t actually break out into open conflict very often (in part because the lower sorts were kept very busy earning enough to live off).<br><br>Maps: the set from ~100,000ya to 2000 BCE.  Covering migration of people to everywhere but New Zealand, Madagascar &amp; the Arctic, development of agriculture &amp; early urbanisation.  I didn&#39;t know that agriculture developed in Papua New Guinea that early.<br><br>Listening<br>Podcasts: ep B36-B43 of The Ancient World podcast - I&#39;m up to date with where he&#39;s got to now.  Don&#39;t think that&#39;s the end of the sequence, although he has got to Xenobia and how you can&#39;t actually quite tie her into the descendants of Cleopatra (which he discovered whilst researching this).<br><br>ep 96-98 of The History of English podcast - up to date with this again.  He&#39;s been looking at the end of John&#39;s reign, and amongst other things words to do with charters and words to do with debate.<br><br>Sunday podcast: first two episodes of Our Man in the Middle East - Jeremy Bowen presenting a history of the modern Middle East as he&#39;s seen it through his over 25 years of reporting on it.  Started with the first Iraq War in 1990, which is just before I really started to pay attention to current affairs, I mean, I knew there was a war in Iraq at the time but I was more worried about my GCSE results.<br><br>Music: while running I&#39;ve listened to a metal compilation called Corrosion, the Spawn soundtrack and the first CD of 100 Hits Rock.<br><br>While sewing I listened to an HMV Playlist CD from June 04 which was mostly unmemorable (there was a track by a band called Bell x1 on it, that was one of the unmemorable ones).  Also an EP by Bella, which reminded me a little of Sarah McLachlan in terms of genre.  And several things by Belle &amp; Sebastien, we have half a dozen singles &amp; two albums. I&#39;d forgotten I like their stuff.<br><br>Games:<br>Diablo 3 - got our characters up to level 50 and finished the first Chapter of the season.<br><br>Watching<br>ep 2 of Secrets of Silicon Valley - how the tech developed in order to target ads better is also being used to manipulate us and has a significant effect on modern politics.  And how you can pretty much be uniquely identified by your facebook likes/browsing habits in order to make this targeting work - they don&#39;t know who you are in the sense of having your street address, but they do know who you are in terms of your personality etc.  This is the obvious case of unintended social consequences of what Silicon Valley is developing coming back to bite the hand that made it - facebook &amp; other social media giants actively helped the Trump campaign but they aren&#39;t personally pleased with the result.  Despite buying that there&#39;s a problem I still thought the presenter was far too keen to fling out the baby with the bathwater.  But I&#39;ve no good ideas for solutions either.<br><br>ep 2 of From Russia to Iran - Levison Wood travelling through the Caucasus, which is mostly visiting countries that the FO thinks one shouldn&#39;t.  This episode include the Dagestan region of Russia &amp; Azerbaijan.  I think I forgot to mention we watched ep 1 last week.  We really enjoyed his Walking the Nile series, and this series is shaping up to be as good.<br><br>ep 1 of My Family, Partition &amp; Me: India 1947 - Partition was 70 years ago, so there are several BBC programmes about it, I&#39;ve recorded two or three of them but not the whole lot.  This series looks at 4 families &amp; their experience of Partition via a family member revisiting the scene.  This ep had a Hindu family who fled a village in what became Bangladesh, a Muslim family who fled from the bit of the Punjab that didn&#39;t become Pakistan, and a British Colonial family whose pater familias remained to help efforts to stop the violence.  Every bit as depressing as you might expect.<br><br>ep 1 of Yorkshire Wolds Way - Paul Rose walking the Wolds Way, just two half hour episodes, fluffy feel good travel TV -  this one was a good antidote to the depression of Partition.<br><br>How to Make a Number One Record - the BBC making good use of their archive footage of music. ,{"33558957":["","","","Margaret Patterson","",1504099415961,"http://www.google.com/favicon.ico",null,"z13oz53qusn5gjajw04ce3h5wnrtszshdes","","s:updates:esshare",null,null,"",null,null,"117776939923543872977",null,"https://lh3.googleusercontent.com/-BvKnrC4OvV8/AAAAAAAAAAI/AAAAAAAAK3c/alaXJjTGW78/photo.jpg",null,"Wednesday media consumption roundup...\n\nBooks\nFiction: finished \"Girl Reading\", Katie Ward. I enjoyed this, each of the \nvignettes was long enough to be a satisfying story, and characters were all \nvery distinct. I did lose the thread a bit in the last one tho, so while I \nhad a sense that it was all supposed to cohere into one thing it didn't \nquite gel for me. Started reading \"Reamde\", Neal Stephenson, so a bit of \nmental whiplash from the change of style ;) (I'm reading my way through a \nsmall handful of books we bought a while ago that I haven't read).\n\nNon-fiction: still reading Gerald Harriss's \"Shaping the Nation: England \n1360-1461\" - tensions between the leadership of the towns \u0026 the general \npopulace, and how this didn't actually break out into open conflict very \noften (in part because the lower sorts were kept very busy earning enough \nto live off).\n\nMaps: the set from ~100,000ya to 2000 BCE. Covering migration of people to \neverywhere but New Zealand, Madagascar \u0026 the Arctic, development of \nagriculture \u0026 early urbanisation. I didn't know that agriculture developed \nin Papua New Guinea that early.\n\nListening\nPodcasts: ep B36-B43 of The Ancient World podcast - I'm up to date with \nwhere he's got to now. Don't think that's the end of the sequence, although \nhe has got to Xenobia and how you can't actually quite tie her into the \ndescendants of Cleopatra (which he discovered whilst researching this).\n\nep 96-98 of The History of English podcast - up to date with this again. \nHe's been looking at the end of John's reign, and amongst other things \nwords to do with charters and words to do with debate.\n\nSunday podcast: first two episodes of Our Man in the Middle East - Jeremy \nBowen presenting a history of the modern Middle East as he's seen it \nthrough his over 25 years of reporting on it. Started with the first Iraq \nWar in 1990, which is just before I really started to pay attention to \ncurrent affairs, I mean, I knew there was a war in Iraq at the time but I \nwas more worried about my GCSE results.\n\nMusic: while running I've listened to a metal compilation called Corrosion, \nthe Spawn soundtrack and the first CD of 100 Hits Rock.\n\nWhile sewing I listened to an HMV Playlist CD from June 04 which was mostly \nunmemorable (there was a track by a band called Bell x1 on it, that was one \nof the unmemorable ones). Also an EP by Bella, which reminded me a little \nof Sarah McLachlan in terms of genre. And several things by Belle \u0026 \nSebastien, we have half a dozen singles \u0026 two albums. I'd forgotten I like \ntheir stuff.\n\nGames:\nDiablo 3 - got our characters up to level 50 and finished the first Chapter \nof the season.\n\nWatching\nep 2 of Secrets of Silicon Valley - how the tech developed in order to \ntarget ads better is also being used to manipulate us and has a significant \neffect on modern politics. And how you can pretty much be uniquely \nidentified by your facebook likes/browsing habits in order to make this \ntargeting work - they don't know who you are in the sense of having your \nstreet address, but they do know who you are in terms of your personality \netc. This is the obvious case of unintended social consequences of what \nSilicon Valley is developing coming back to bite the hand that made it - \nfacebook \u0026 other social media giants actively helped the Trump campaign but \nthey aren't personally pleased with the result. Despite buying that there's \na problem I still thought the presenter was far too keen to fling out the \nbaby with the bathwater. But I've no good ideas for solutions either.\n\nep 2 of From Russia to Iran - Levison Wood travelling through the Caucasus, \nwhich is mostly visiting countries that the FO thinks one shouldn't. This \nepisode include the Dagestan region of Russia \u0026 Azerbaijan. I think I \nforgot to mention we watched ep 1 last week. We really enjoyed his Walking \nthe Nile series, and this series is shaping up to be as good.\n\nep 1 of My Family, Partition \u0026 Me: India 1947 - Partition was 70 years ago, \nso there are several BBC programmes about it, I've recorded two or three of \nthem but not the whole lot. This series looks at 4 families \u0026 their \nexperience of Partition via a family member revisiting the scene. This ep \nhad a Hindu family who fled a village in what became Bangladesh, a Muslim \nfamily who fled from the bit of the Punjab that didn't become Pakistan, and \na British Colonial family whose pater familias remained to help efforts to \nstop the violence. Every bit as depressing as you might expect.\n\nep 1 of Yorkshire Wolds Way - Paul Rose walking the Wolds Way, just two \nhalf hour episodes, fluffy feel good travel TV - this one was a good \nantidote to the depression of Partition.\n\nHow to Make a Number One Record - the BBC making good use of their archive \nfootage of music. A bit of a shallow programme but fun to watch - more of a \nretrospective than any attempt at analysis.","+MargaretPatterson/posts/jBes7nczGaU",0,0.0,"./+MargaretPatterson",null,null,null,"",false,0,false,true,null,false,true,null,false,1504099415961,null,null,false,null,null,null,false,null,null,null,null,null,null,false,false,null,null,false,null,null,null,null,false,null,null,null,null,null,null,null,null,null,null,null,["4/jcsnavvuaotr2xfnhsuqiun1hdvn0h33gotqkhfrhttbcwvuihoactfn/",4,null,null,null,null,1.504128639869E12,null,null,null,null,null,null,false,null,null,3,null,false]

,[0,"ep 2 of Secrets of Silicon Valley - how the tech developed in order to target ads better is also being used to manipulate us and has a significant effect on modern politics.  And how you can pretty much be uniquely identified by your facebook likes/browsing habits in order to make this targeting work - they don't know who you are in the sense of having your street address, but they do know who you are in terms of your personality etc.  This is the obvious case of unintended social consequences of what Silicon Valley is developing coming back to bite the hand that made it - facebook \u0026 other social media giants actively helped the Trump campaign but they aren't personally pleased with the result.  Despite buying that there's a problem I still thought the presenter was far too keen to fling out the baby with the bathwater.  But I've no good ideas for solutions either."]

We really enjoyed his Walking the Nile series, and this series is shaping up to be as good."]

,[0,"ep 1 of My Family, Partition \u0026 Me: India 1947 - Partition was 70 years ago, so there are several BBC programmes about it, I've recorded two or three of them but not the whole lot.  This series looks at 4 families \u0026 their experience of Partition via a family member revisiting the scene.  This ep had a Hindu family who fled a village in what became Bangladesh, a Muslim family who fled from the bit of the Punjab that didn't become Pakistan, and a British Colonial family whose pater familias remained to help efforts to stop the violence.  Every bit as depressing as you might expect."]
